# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust Borrow Checker MIR Analysis Chain

## Your Task

Trace how the Rust borrow checker analyzes MIR (Mid-level IR) in rust-lang/rust. Find Rust source files implementing: the MIR borrow check entry point, the place conflict detection, the live range calculation, and the two-phase borrow resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7` (rust-lang/rust)
- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

{"content":"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n5: //!\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n8: //!\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\n10: //! ```text\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n13: //! ```\n14: //!\n15: //! Then our steps are:\n16: //! ```text\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\n22: //! ```\n23: //!\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n26: //!\n27: //! ```text\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\n30: //! ```\n31: //!\n32: //! Then our steps are:\n33: //! ```text\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n37: //! ```\n38: //!\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\n40: //! is a fu
... (truncated)

## Key Components Identified:

**Entry Point & Dispatching:**
- `mir_borrowck` (lib.rs:117) - The main query provider
- `do_mir_borrowck` (root_cx.rs:242) - Processes all nested bodies
- `borrowck_collect_region_constraints` (lib.rs:309) - Main analysis orchestrator

**Type Checking & Constraint Generation:**
- `type_check` (type_check/mod.rs:98) - MIR type checking and constraint generation

**Live Range Calculation:**
- `type_check/liveness/generate` (type_check/liveness/mod.rs) - Initiates liveness analysis
- `trace` (type_check/liveness/trace.rs) - Computes liveness by backtracking through CFG

**Place Conflict Detection:**
- `places_conflict` (places_conflict.rs:81) - Helper for checking place conflicts
- `borrow_conflicts_with_place` (places_conflict.rs:104) - Core conflict analysis by iterating through place projections

**Two-Phase Borrow Resolution:**
- `check_activations` (lib.rs:1823) - Validates two-phase borrow activations
- `TwoPhaseActivation` (borrow_set.rs) - Tracks activation locations

**NLL Region Computation:**
- `compute_regions` (nll.rs:113) - Non-lexical lifetimes computation
- `RegionInferenceContext` (region_infer/mod.rs:79) - Region inference engine
- `solve` (region_infer/mod.rs:493) - Constraint solving via SCC propagation
- `LivenessValues` (region_infer/values.rs:41) - Liveness information storage

The 0th\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n237:     /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n238:     Region(ty::RegionVid),\n239: }\n240: \n241: /// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n242: ///\n243: /// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n244: /// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n245: /// a query response.\n246: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n247: pub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n248:     inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n249: }\n250: // DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n251: // type is not recognized as a binder for late-bound region.\n252: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeVisitable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n253: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeFoldable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n254: \n255: impl<'tcx> ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n256:     /// All regions of `ty` must be of kind `ReVar` and must represent\n257:     /// universal regions *external* to the closure.\n258:     pub fn bind(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n259:         let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n260:             ty::ReVar(vid) => {\n261:                 let br = ty::BoundRegion {\n262:                     var: ty::BoundVar::from_usize(vid.index()),\n263:                     kind: ty::BoundRegionKind::Anon,\n264:                 };\n265:                 ty::Region::new_bound(tcx, depth, br)\n266:             }\n267:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region in ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy: {r:?}\"),\n268:         });\n269: \n270:         Self { inner }\n271:     }\n272: \n273:     pub fn instantiate(\n274:         self,\n275:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n276:         mut map: impl FnMut(ty::RegionVid) -> ty::Region<'tcx>,\n277:     ) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n278:         fold_regions(tcx, self.inner, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n279:             ty::ReBound(ty::BoundVarIndexKind::Bound(debruijn), br) => {\n280:                 debug_assert_eq!(debruijn, depth);\n281:                 map(ty::RegionVid::from_usize(br.var.index()))\n282:             }\n283:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region {r:?}\"),\n284:         })\n285:     }\n286: }\n287: \n288: struct CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n289:     infcx: BorrowckInferCtxt<'tcx>,\n290:     body_owned: Body<'tcx>,\n291:     promoted: IndexVec<Promoted, Body<'tcx>>,\n292:     move_data: MoveData<'tcx>,\n293:     borrow_set: BorrowSet<'tcx>,\n294: This initializes the relevant data structures\n308: /// and then type checks the MIR body.\n309: fn borrowck_collect_region_constraints<'tcx>(\n310:     root_cx: &mut BorrowCheckRootCtxt<'tcx>,\n311:     def: LocalDefId,\n312: ) -> CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n313:     let tcx = root_cx.tcx;\n314:     let infcx = BorrowckInferCtxt::new(tcx, def, root_cx.root_def_id());\n315:     let (input_body, promoted) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n316:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n317:     let input_promoted: &IndexSlice<_, _> = &promoted.borrow();\n318:     if let Some(e) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n319:         infcx.set_tainted_by_errors(e);\n320:         root_cx.set_tainted_by_errors(e);\n321:     }\n322: \n323:     // Replace all regions with fresh inference variables. This\n324:     // requires first making our own copy of the MIR. This copy will\n325:     // be modified (in place) to contain non-lexical lifetimes. It\n326:     // will have a lifetime tied to the inference context.\n327:     let mut body_owned = input_body.clone();\n328:     let mut promoted = input_promoted.to_owned();\n329:     let Debug)]\n1041: enum ArtificialField {\n1042:     ArrayLength,\n1043:     FakeBorrow,\n1044: }\n1045: \n1046: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1047: enum AccessDepth {\n1048:     /// From Shallow(Option<ArtificialField>),\n1054: \n1055:     /// From the RFC: \"A *deep* access means that all data reachable\n1056:     /// through the given place may be invalidated or accesses by\n1057:     /// this action.\"\n1058:     Deep,\n1059: \n1060:     /// Access is Deep only when there is a Drop implementation that\n1061:     /// can reach the data behind the reference.\n1062:     Drop,\n1063: }\n1064: \n1065: /// Kind of access to a value: read or write\n1066: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1067: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1068: enum ReadOrWrite {\n1069:     /// From the RFC: \"A *read* means that the existing data may be\n1070:     /// read, but will not be changed.\"\n1071:     Read(ReadKind),\n1072: \n1073:     /// From the RFC: \"A Write(WriteKind),\n1077: \n1078:     /// For two-phase borrows, we distinguish a reservation (which is treated\n1079:     /// like a Read) from an activation (which is treated like a write), \n1168: impl<'a, 'tcx> MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n1169:     fn body(&self) -> &'a Body<'tcx> {\n1170:         self.body\n1171:     }\n1172: \n1173:     /// Checks an access to the given place to Examines the set of borrows\n1174:     /// that are in scope, as well as which paths have been initialized, to ensure that (a) the\n1175:     /// place is initialized and (b) it is not borrowed in some way that would prevent this\n1176:     /// access.\n1177:     ///\n1178:     /// Returns `true` if an error is reported.\n1179:     fn access_place(\n1180:         &mut self,\n1181:         location: Location,\n1182:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1183:         kind: (AccessDepth, ReadOrWrite),\n1184:         is_local_mutation_allowed: LocalMutationIsAllowed,\n1185:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1186:     ) {\n1187:         let (sd, rw) = kind;\n1188: \n1189:         if let Activation(_, borrow_index) = rw {\n1190:             if       \"access_place: suppressing error place_span=`{:?}` kind=`{:?}`\",\n1207:                 place_span, kind\n1208:             );\n1209:             return;\n1210:         }\n1211: \n1212: location,\n1218:         );\n1219:         let conflict_error = self.check_access_for_conflict(location, place_span, sd, rw, state);\n1220: \n1221:         if conflict_error || mutability_error {\n1222:             debug!(\"access_place: logging error place_span=`{:?}` kind=`{:?}`\", place_span, kind);\n1223:             self.access_place_error_reported.insert((place_span.0, place_span.1));\n1224:         }\n1225:     }\n1226: \n1227:     fn borrows_in_scope<'s>(\n1228:         &self,\n1229:         location: Location,\n1230:         state: &'s BorrowckDomain,\n1231:     ) -> Cow<'s, MixedBitSet<BorrowIndex>> {\n1232:         if let Some(polonius) = &self.polonius_output {\n1233:             // Use polonius output if it has been enabled.\n1234:             let Cow::Borrowed(&state.borrows)\n1242:         }\n1243:     }\n1244: \n1245:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1246:     fn check_access_for_conflict(\n1247:         &mut self,\n1248:         location: Location,\n1249:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1250:         sd: AccessDepth,\n1251:         rw: ReadOrWrite,\n1252:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1253:     ) -> bool {\n1254:         let mut error_reported = false;\n1255: \n1256:         let borrows_in_scope = self.borrows_in_scope(location, state);\n1257: \n1258: //\n1270:                 // NOTE: *reservations* do conflict with themselves;\n1271:                 // thus aren't injecting unsoundness w/ this check.)\n1272:                 (Activation(_,           (borrow_index, borrow),\n1280:                     );\n1281:                     ControlFlow::Continue(())\n1282:                 }\n1283: \n1284:                 (Read(_), \n1301:                 (Read(kind), BorrowKind::Mut { .. }) => {\n1302:                     // Reading from mere reservations of mutable-borrows is OK.\n1303:                     if      }\n1370:             },\n1371:         );\n1372: \n1373:         error_reported\n1374:     }\n1375: \n1376:     /// Through #123739, `BackwardIncompatibleDropHint`s (BIDs) are introduced.\n1377:     /// We would like to emit lints whether borrow checking fails at these future drop locations.\n1378:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1379:     fn check_backward_incompatible_drop(\n1380:         &mut self,\n1381:         location: Location,\n1382:         place: Place<'tcx>,\n1383:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1384:     ) {\n1385:   fn mutate_place(\n1432:         &mut self,\n1433:         location: Location,\n1434:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1435:         kind: AccessDepth,\n1436:         state:      state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1455:     ) {\n1456:         match rvalue {\n1457:             &Rvalue::Ref(_ /*rgn*/, bk, place) => {\n1458:                 let access_kind = match bk {\n1459: Current body is a nested closure, and we are modifying path starting from\n1609:             //    a Place captured by our parent closure.\n1610: \n1611:             // Handle (c), the path being modified is exactly the path captured by our parent\n1612:             if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place.as_ref()) {\n1613:                 this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1614:                 return;\n1615:             }\n1616: \n1617:             for (place_ref, proj) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n1618:                 //     // when generating MIR.\n1642:         match *operand {\n1643:             Operand::Move(place) | Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1644:                 match place.as_local() {\n1645:             // closure from a shared reference.\n1661:                         //\n1662:                         // As such we have to search for the local that this\n1663:                         // {}\n1703:         }\n1704:     }\n1705: \n1706:     fn consume_operand(\n1707:         &mut self,\n1708:         location: Location,\n1709:         (operand, span): (&Operand<'tcx>, Span),\n1710: #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self))]\n1760:     fn check_for_invalidation_at_exit(\n1761:         &mut self,\n1762:         location: Location,\n1763:         borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\n1764: check_movable_place(&mut self, location: Location, place: Place<'tcx>) {\n1850:         use IllegalMoveOriginKind::*;\n1851: \n1852:         let body = self.body;\n1853:         let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n1854:         let mut place_ty = PlaceTy::from_ty(body.local_decls[place.local].ty);\n1855:         for (place_ref, elem) in place.iter_projections() {\n1856:             match elem fn check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n1982:         &mut self,\n1983:         location: Location,\n1984:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n1985:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n1986:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1987:     ) {\n1988:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n1989: \n1990:         // Bad scenarios:\n1991:         //\n1992:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c`\n1993:         // 2. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c.d` (without first reinitializing `a.b.c.d`)\n1994:         // 3. Uninitialized `(a.b.c: &_)`, use of `*a.b.c`; note that with\n1995:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n1996:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n1997:         //\n1998:         // OK scenarios:\n1999:         //\n2000:         // 4. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2001:         // 5. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2002:         // 6. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2003:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2004:         // 7. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2005: \n2006:         // The dataflow tracks shallow prefixes distinctly (that is,\n2007:         // field-accesses on P distinctly from P itself), in order to\n2008:         // track substructure initialization separately from the whole\n2009:         // structure.\n2010:         //\n2011:         // E.g., when looking at (*a.b.c).d, if the closest prefix for\n2012:         // which we have a MovePath is `a.b`, then that means that the\n2013:         // initialization state of `a.b` is all we need to inspect to\n2014:         // know if `a.b.c` is valid (and from that we infer that the\n2015:         // dereference and `.d` access is also valid, since we assume\n2016:         // `a.b.c` is assigned a reference to an initialized and\n2017:         // well-formed record structure.)\n2018: \n2019:         // Therefore, if we seek out the *closest* prefix for which we\n2020:         // have a MovePath, that should capture the initialization\n2021:         // state for the place scenario.\n2022:         //\n2023:         // This code covers scenarios 1, 2, and 3.\n2024: \n2025:         debug!(\"check_if_full_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2026:         let (prefix, mpi) = self.move_path_closest_to(place_span.0);\n2027:         if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2028:             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2029:                 location,\n2030:                 desired_action,\n2031:                 (prefix, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2032:                 mpi,\n2033:             );\n2034:         } // Only query longest prefix with a MovePath, not further\n2035:         // ancestors; dataflow recurs on children when parents\n2036:         // move (to support partial (re)inits).\n2037:         //\n2038:         // (I.e., querying parents breaks scenario 7; but may want\n2039:         // to do such a query based on partial-init feature-gate.)\n2040:     }\n2041: \n2042:     /// Subslices correspond to multiple move paths, so we iterate through the\n2043:     /// elements of the base array. For each element we check\n2044:     ///\n2045:     /// * Does this element overlap with our slice.\n2046:     /// * Is any part of it uninitialized.\n2047:     fn check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2048:         &mut self,\n2049:         location: Location,\n2050:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2051:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2052:         maybe_uninits: &MixedBitSet<MovePathIndex>,\n2053:         from: u64,\n2054:         to: u64,\n2055:     ) {\n2056:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2057:             let move_paths = &self.move_data.move_paths;\n2058: \n2059:             let root_path = &move_paths[mpi];\n2060:             for (child_mpi, child_move_path) in root_path.children(move_paths) {\n2061:                 let last_proj = child_move_path.place.projection.last().unwrap();\n2062:                 if let ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, from_end, .. } = last_proj {\n2063:                     debug_assert!(!from_end, \"Array constant indexing shouldn't be `from_end`.\");\n2064: \n2065:                     if (from..to).contains(offset) {\n2066:                         let uninit_child =\n2067:                             self.move_data.find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(child_mpi, |mpi| {\n2068:                                 maybe_uninits.contains(mpi)\n2069:                             });\n2070: \n2071:                         if let Some(uninit_child) = uninit_child {\n2072:                             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2073:                                 location,\n2074:                                 desired_action,\n2075:                                 (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2076:                                 uninit_child,\n2077:                             );\n2078:                             return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2079:                         }\n2080:                     }\n2081:                 }\n2082:             }\n2083:         }\n2084:     }\n2085: \n2086:     fn check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2087:         &mut self,\n2088:         location: Location,\n2089:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2090:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2091:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2092:     ) {\n2093:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2094: \n2095:         // Bad scenarios:\n2096:         //\n2097:         // 1. For example it will currently filter out\n2158:     /// places that are Copy; thus we do not track places of shared\n2159:     /// reference type. This routine will walk up a place along its\n2160:     /// prefixes, searching for a foundational place that *is*\n2161:     /// tracked in the MoveData.\n2162:     ///\n2163:     /// An Err result includes a tag indicated why the search failed.\n2164:     /// Currently this can only occur if the place is built off of a\n2165:     /// static variable, as we do not track those in the LookupResult::Parent(Some(mpi)) | LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => {\n2169:                 (self.move_data.move_paths[mpi].place.as_ref(), mpi)\n2170:             }\n2171:             LookupResult::Parent(None) => panic!(\"should have move path for every Local\"),\n2172:         }\n2173:     }\n2174: \n2175:     fn move_path_for_place(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> => Some(mpi),\n2183:         }\n2184:     }\n2185: \n2186:     fn check_if_assigned_path_is_moved(\n2187:         &mut self,\n2188:         location: Location,\n2189:         (place, span): ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => {\n2208:                     check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2209:                 }\n2210: \n2211:                 // further)\n2218:                     break;\n2219:                 }\n2220: \n2221:                 ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. } => {\n2222:                     panic!(\"we don't allow assignments to subslices, location: {location:?}\");\n2223:                 }\n2224: \n2225:                 ProjectionElem::Field(..) => {\n2226:                     // if type of `P` has a dtor, then\n2227:                     // assigning to `P.f` requires `P` itself\n2228:                     // be already initialized\n2229:                     let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n2230:                     let    self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2234:                                 location, InitializationRequiringAction::Assignment,\n2235:                                 (place_base, span),          }\n2241: \n2242:                         // Once `let s; s.x = V; read(s.x);`,\n2243:                         // is allowed, remove this match arm.\n2244:                         ty::Adt(..) | ty::Tuple(..) => {\n2245:                             check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2246:                         }\n2247: \n2248:                         _ => {}\n2249:                     }\n2250:                 }\n2251:             }\n2252:         }\n2253: \n2254:         fn check_parent_of_field<'a, 'tcx>(\n2255:             this: &mut MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx>,\n2256:             location: Location,\n2257:             base: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n2258:             span: Span,\n2259:             state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2260:         ) {\n2261:             // rust-lang/rust#21232: Until Rust allows reads from the\n2262:             // initialized parts of partially initialized structs, we\n2263:             // will, starting with          //\n2268:             // 1. `let mut s; s.x = Val; read(s.x);`\n2269:             //\n2270:             // we will for now disallow this:\n2271:             //\n2272:             // 2. `let mut s; s.x = Val;`\n2273:             //\n2274:             // and also this:\n2275:             //\n2276:             // 3. `let mut s = ...; drop(s); s.x=Val;`\n2277:             //\n2278:             // This does not use check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved,\n2279:             // because we want to *allow* reinitializations of fields:\n2280:             // e.g., want to allow\n2281:             //\n2282:             // `let mut s = ...; drop(s.x); s.x=Val;`\n2283:             //\n2284:             // This does not use check_if_full_path_is_moved on\n2285:             // `base`, because that would report an error about the\n2286:             // `base` as a whole, but in this scenario we *really*\n2287:             // want to report an error about the actual thing that was\n2288:             // moved, which may be some prefix of `base`.\n2289: \n2290:             // Shallow so that we'll stop at any dereference; we'll\n2291:             // report errors about issues with such bases elsewhere.\n2292:             let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2293: \n2294:             // Find the shortest uninitialized prefix you can reach\n2295:             // without going over a Deref.\n2296:             let mut shortest_uninit_seen = None;\n2297:             for prefix in this.prefixes(base, PrefixSet::Shallow) {\n2298:                 let Some(mpi) = \"check_parent_of_field updating shortest_uninit_seen from {:?} to {:?}\",\n2303:                         shortest_uninit_seen,\n2304:                         Some((prefix, mpi))\n2305:                     );\n2306:                     shortest_uninit_seen = Some((prefix, mpi));\n2307:                 } else {\n2308:                     debug!(\"check_parent_of_field {:?} is definitely initialized\", (prefix, mpi));\n2309:                 }\n2310:             }\n2311: \n2312:             if let Some((prefix, mpi)) = shortest_uninit_seen {\n2313:                 // Check for a reassignment into an uninitialized field of a union (for example,\n2314:                 // after a move out). In this case, do not report an error here. There is an\n2315:                 // exception, if this is the first assignment into the union (that is, there is\n2316:                 // no move out from an earlier location) then this is an this.body)\n2322:                     })\n2323:                 {\n2324:                     return;\n2325:                 }\n2326: \n2327:    }\n2339:         }\n2340:     }\n2341: \n2342:     /// Checks the permissions for the given place and read or write kind\n2343:     ///\n2344:     /// Returns `true` if an error is reported.\n2345:     fn check_access_permissions(\n2346:         &mut self,\n2347:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2348:         kind: ReadOrWrite,\n2349:         is_local_mutation_allowed: LocalMutationIsAllowed,\n2350:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2351:         location: Location,\n2352:     ) -> bool {\n2353:         debug!(\n2354:             \"check_access_permissions({:?}, {:?}, is_local_mutation_allowed: {:?})\",\n2355:             place, kind, is_local_mutation_allowed\n2356:         );\n2357: \n2358:         let error_access;\n2359:         let the_place_err;\n2360: kind: mut_borrow_kind })) => {\n2364:                 let is_local_mutation_allowed = match mut_borrow_kind {\n2365:                     // `ClosureCapture` is used for mutable variable with an immutable binding.\n2366:                     // This is only behaviour difference between `ClosureCapture` and mutable\n2367:                     // borrows.\n2368:                     MutBorrowKind::ClosureCapture => LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n2369:                     MutBorrowKind::Default | MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow => {\n2370:                         is_local_mutation_allowed\n2371:                     }\n2372:                 };\n2373:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2374:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2375:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2376:                         return false;\n2377:                     }\n2378:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2379:                         error_access = AccessKind::MutableBorrow;\n2380:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2381:                     }\n2382:                 }\n2383:             }\n2384:             Reservation(WriteKind::Mutate) | Write(WriteKind::Mutate) => {\n2385:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2386:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2387:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2388:                         return false;\n2389:                     }\n2390:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2391:                         error_access = AccessKind::Mutate;\n2392:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2393:                     }\n2394:                 }\n2395:             }\n2396: \n2397:             Reservation(\n2398:                 WriteKind::Move\n2399:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2400:                 | WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop\n2401:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Shared)\n2402:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Fake(_)),\n2403:             )\n2404: The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //!
